# RPCE Practice Questions (generated, RONR 12th-ed.-grounded)

1000 questions generated from the transcribed *Robert's Rules of Order Newly Revised, 12th ed.* corpus. Every answer cites the exact section and quotes it verbatim. Question types are varied (cloze recall, quote→section, and stated-in-section), following the style of [`RPCE-Sample-Questions-v4-100625.md`](./RPCE-Sample-Questions-v4-100625.md).

> Reproduce with `python pylib/tools/rpce_generate_questions.py`.

   A. The division of main motions into original and incidental main motions was mentioned in 6 and is discussed below.
   B. By a single vote, a series of special orders or general orders—or a mixture of both—can be made; such a series is called an agenda.
   C. It is a fundamental principle of parliamentary law that the right to vote is limited to the members of an organization who are actually present at the time the vote is taken in a regular or properly called meeting, although it should be noted that a member need not be present when the question is put.
   D. A Report on a Referred Subject on Which No Resolution or Motion Was Pending.

**Answer Key**

1. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:2](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-2) — "The division of main motions into original and incidental main motions was mentioned in 6 and is discussed below."
2. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [6:12](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-6-12) — "The privileged motions are listed below in ascending order of rank."
3. Answer: **Resolved**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:15](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-15) — "If the resolution is offered in a mass meeting (or in any meeting where there is no established organization whose act the adopted resolution would become), it may begin, “Resolved, That it is the sense of this meeting that…” A resolution can consist of more than one resolving clause, as in the following example:"
4. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:53](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-53) — "A motion to adopt a resolution, bylaws, or any other document can be amended by adding, “and that it be printed and that members be furnished with copies,” or, “that it [or “they”] go into effect at the close of this annual meeting,” or anything of a similar nature (see also 51; for the adoption of bylaws, see…"
5. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [6:5](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-6-5) — "The subsidiary motions, briefly described by function, are as follows:"
6. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [6:3](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-6-3) — "Subsidiary motions assist the assembly in treating or disposing of a main motion (and sometimes other motions)."
7. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [6:16](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-6-16) — "Each of the incidental motions is applicable only in its own type of special circumstance—which may be a particular characteristic present in the motion to which it is incidental, or a particular point in time or possible occurrence during the assembly’s involvement with the other motion or matter."
8. Answer: **agree to**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:52](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-52) — "A motion to adopt (or accept or agree to) an officer’s or a committee’s report or recommendations which the assembly (by means of a main motion) directed the officer or committee to prepare is an incidental main motion."
9. Answer: **Previous Question**. See RONR (12th ed.) [6:11](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-6-11) — "All of them take precedence over motions of any other class (except in certain instances where the immediately pending question may be a motion to Amend, a motion for the Previous Question, or an incidental motion that was moved while a still higher-ranking privileged motion was immediately pending)."
10. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [6:4](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-6-4) — "Each of the subsidiary motions is briefly described below in terms of the type of situation where it is of use, in a manner that may convey a suggestion of how the order of precedence of motions was arrived at."
11. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [6:28](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-6-28) — "(Each of the motions that bring a question again before the assembly is fully discussed in 34–37.)"
12. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:11](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-11) — "A motion whose only effect is to propose that the assembly refrain from doing something should not be offered if the same result can be accomplished by offering no motion at all."
13. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:25](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-25) — "If a single composite proposal for taking a number of actions in reference to a particular subject has too many elements to be conveniently written into one resolution (even of several clauses), it can be set forth in a series of separate resolutions that can be numbered and offered by means of a single main motion,…"
14. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:33](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-33) — "In the latter case, when a motion that takes precedence over all pending questions is made, that motion is disposed of first, and then “the question recurs” on the next-most-recentlymoved motion; that is (as far as applicable in the existing parliamentary situation), its consideration is resumed at the point where the…"
15. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:48](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-48) — "When no question is pending, a member desiring to give a notice is entitled to preference in recognition (but see 42:6–13 for circumstances in which others may have a higher priority for such preference)."
16. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:42](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-42) — "If the assembly is taking up business under the heading of Special Orders in the order of business, or that of Unfinished Business and General Orders (rather than New Business as in the above example), the chair, instead of saying, “Is there further new business,” announces, “The next item of business is… [immediately…"
17. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:1](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-1) — "As explained in 3–6, a main motion is a motion whose introduction brings business before the assembly; such a motion can be made only while no other motion is pending."
18. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:37](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-37) — "Below for the main motion, and in each of the succeeding sections covering the different motions of parliamentary law (11–37), is a subsection headed Form and Example giving a script showing the words to be spoken by a member making the motion and by the chair in stating and putting the question on it."
19. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [6:27](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-6-27) — "The motions that bring a question again before the assembly have a number of differences among themselves, and they may be variously subgrouped depending on the point of view, as follows:"
20. Answer: **preamble**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:16](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-16) — "When special circumstances make it desirable to include a brief statement of background, the motion should be cast in the form of a resolution, with the background or reasons incorporated in a preamble that is placed before the resolving clauses."
21. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:35](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-35) — "A subsidiary or incidental motion adhere to a main question if it is related to the main question in such a way that—once introduced—it must be decided before the main question can be decided."
22. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:30](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-30) — "There are several means by which such a result can be accomplished, depending on the conditions and the degree or scope of the changes desired."
23. Answer: **incidental main motions**. See RONR (12th ed.) [6:2](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-6-2) — "It is usual to distinguish between original main motions and incidental main motions—which differ principally in the nature of their subject matter."
24. Answer: **question of privilege**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:36](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-36) — "As a result of the application of one of these devices to interrupt a pending question, an order of the day (that is, another question previously set as due to come up automatically at the time) may be taken up, or an urgent motion relating to the privileges of the assembly or of a member may be admitted as a question of privilege to be entertained immediately."
25. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:27](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-27) — "Many of the alternative courses for obtaining a result that cannot be directly reached through a main motion, as described above, involve parliamentary motions having special requirements (such as a two-thirds vote or previous notice, 10:44–51) for their adoption."
26. Answer: **motions**. See RONR (12th ed.) [6:15](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-6-15) — "Incidental motions relate, in different ways, to the pending business or to business otherwise at hand—some of them with varying degrees of resemblance to subsidiary motions, but none of them possessing all five of the characteristics listed in 6:6."
27. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:28](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-28) — "The basic procedure by which main motions are introduced and considered is described in detail in 4."
28. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:21](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-21) — "If there is a preamble, each clause, written as a separate paragraph, begins with the word “Whereas” followed by a comma, and the next word should begin with a capital letter."
29. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:19](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-19) — "In the consideration of a resolution having a preamble, the preamble is always amended last, since changes in the resolving clauses may require changes in the preamble."
30. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:43](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-43) — "For examples of the use of subsidiary and incidental motions in the handling of main motions and the application of privileged motions while a main motion is pending, see 11–33.)"
31. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:5](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-5) — "An incidental main motion involving a subject already entered into might be a motion to adopt recommendations which a committee has prepared upon instructions (not relating to a referred motion), or a motion to ratify action taken at a meeting when no quorum was present."
32. Answer: **Amend**. See RONR (12th ed.) [6:9](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-6-9) — "For each of the subsidiary motions Amend, Commit, Postpone Definitely, and Limit or Extend Limits of Debate, there is a corresponding incidental main motion (10:4–5) of the same name that can be made when no other motion is pending."
33. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:57](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-57) — "Since the motion to ratify (or to censure) is a main motion, it is debatable and opens the entire question to debate."
34. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:3](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-3) — "An original main motion is a main motion that introduces a substantive question as a new subject."
35. Answer: **previous notice**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:44](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-44) — "The term previous notice (or notice), as applied to necessary conditions for the adoption of certain motions, has a particular meaning in parliamentary law."
36. Answer: **Amend**. See RONR (12th ed.) [6:8](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-6-8) — "The four lowest-ranking subsidiary motions can be debated (except that Amend is undebatable when it is applied to an undebatable motion)."
37. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [6:17](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-6-17) — "The order in which the incidental motions are listed below, unlike that in which the subsidiary and privileged motions are presented above, has no relation to what other motions they may take precedence over or yield to (see discussion beginning in 6:18)."
38. Answer: **at a meeting**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:47](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-47) — "If previous notice is given at a meeting, it can be given orally unless the rules of the organization require it to be in writing—which is often the case with notice of amendments to bylaws."
39. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [6:18](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-6-18) — "Conditions Under Which Incidental Motions Take Precedence over, or Yield to, Other Motions."
40. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [6:7](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-6-7) — "Cases Where One Subsidiary Motion Can Be Applied to Another."
41. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:51](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-51) — "Instead of being given at a meeting, a notice can also be sent to every member with the call of the meeting at which the matter is to come up for action, in cases where there is a duty or established custom of issuing such a call."
42. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:34](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-34) — "This principle may be illustrated by a somewhat more complicated example than may ordinarily occur in practice."
43. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:56](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-56) — "A motion to ratify can be amended by substituting a motion of censure, and vice versa, when the action involved has been taken by an officer or other representative of the assembly."
44. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [6:22](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-6-22) — "While a series consisting of a main motion and a number of subsidiary or privileged motions is being considered, it is possible for some of the incidental motions—such as a Point of Order, an Appeal, or a Division of the Assembly—to arise more than once, in connection with different motions in the series."
45. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [6:25](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-6-25) — "Four motions are grouped in this book as motions that bring a question again before the assembly since, either by their adoption or by their introduction, they allow the assembly to consider again the merits of a question that has previously been disposed of in some way."
46. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:31](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-31) — "Introduction of Subsidiary or Incidental Motions as a Part of—or Privileged Motions as an Interruption of—the Consideration of a Main Motion."
47. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:6](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-6) — "The chief difference in the rules governing original and incidental main motions is that an Objection to the Consideration of a Question (26) can be applied only to original main and not to incidental main motions."
48. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:40](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-40) — "The chair immediately turns toward Member A (who resumed his seat after making his motion) to see if he wishes the floor first in debate (see 3:33(1))."
49. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [6:23](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-6-23) — "Incidental Main Motions Corresponding to Incidental Motions."
50. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:12](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-12) — "It is preferable to avoid a motion containing a negative statement even in cases where the effect of the motion is to propose that something be done, since members may become confused as to the effect of voting for or against such a motion."

**Answer Key**

1. Answer: **unanimous consent**. See RONR (12th ed.) [12:45](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-12-45) — "Amendments are sometimes so simple or acceptable that they may be adopted by unanimous consent (see 4:58–63)."
2. Answer: **meeting**. See RONR (12th ed.) [14:5](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-14-5) — "Rules limiting the time to which a question can be postponed are related to the terms meeting and session (8), as follows:"
3. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [11:6](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-11-6) — "Assume that the following resolution is pending in a meeting of a local unit of a state professional society:"
4. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [21:13](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-21-13) — "Since a motion to Adjourn may be voted down because a majority wish to hear one speech or take one vote, this motion must be renewable as soon as there has been any progress in business or even material progress in debate."
5. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [12:33](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-12-33) — "In stating the question on each motion in any series involving amendments, and again when putting the motion to a vote, the chair should take care that the members understand which motion is under immediate consideration, as well as the effect of adopting or rejecting it."
6. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [17:6](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-17-6) — "After a question has been laid on the table, it can be taken from the table by a majority vote as soon as the interrupting business is disposed of—or at some later time before the limits for taking it from the table have expired (see below)— whenever no question is pending, provided that business of the same class as…"
7. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [12:17](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-12-17) — "Aside from these principles, there is no single, all-inclusive test for determining when a proposed amendment is germane and when it is not."
8. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [15:11](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-15-11) — "After the adoption of an order that does provide a time for closing debate on the main question—either at a specified hour or after debate for a specified length of time, as in Form and Example (b) or (f) below—motions to Commit or to Postpone to a Certain Time are not in order, since providing a time for closing…"
9. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [16:17](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-16-17) — "Reconsideration of a Vote While the Previous Question Is in Effect."
10. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [13:2](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-13-2) — "The motion to Commit also has three variations whose object is not to turn the main question over to a smaller group, but to permit the assembly’s full meeting body to consider it with the greater freedom of debate that is allowed in committees—that is, with no limit on the number of times a member can speak."
11. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [17:20](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-17-20) — "“I move to lay the question on the table”; or “I move that the resolution be laid on the table.” (It is preferable to avoid moving “to table” a motion, or “that the motion be tabled.”)"
12. Answer: **Previous Question**. See RONR (12th ed.) [17:12](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-17-12) — "If debate has been closed by ordering the Previous Question or by the expiration of the time to which debate was limited, then up until the moment of taking the last vote under the order, the questions still before the assembly can be laid on the table."
13. Answer: **Previous Question**. See RONR (12th ed.) [16:16](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-16-16) — "In practice, if a motion to reconsider an affirmative vote on the Previous Question prevails, the vote that adopted the motion to Reconsider is also presumed to have carried out the reconsideration and to have reversed the vote that is reconsidered."
14. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [20:8](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-20-8) — "“I move that the meeting recess [or “take a recess”] until 2 P.M.”;"
15. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [14:19](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-14-19) — "When consideration of a postponed question is resumed at a later session, any orders limiting or extending the limits of debate or for the Previous Question that were adopted at the original session are exhausted (see 15:18, 16:11–12), and debate takes place according to the regular rules."
16. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [14:16](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-14-16) — "The full rules regarding the priority of orders of the day, and their relation to each other and to the order of business, are given in 41."
17. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [21:1](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-21-1) — "A motion to adjourn may be a privileged or a main motion depending on a number of conditions."
18. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [14:11](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-14-11) — "It is not in order, either through a subsidiary motion or a main motion, to postpone a class of business composed of several items or subjects, such as reports of officers or reports of committees (see Order of Business, 41); but each report can be postponed separately as it is announced or called for."
19. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [12:96](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-12-96) — "When a blank exists or has been created, the chair calls for suggestions, by asking for them in a manner appropriate to the particular question, such as by asking, “How many members shall the committee consist of?”; or, “In the pending resolution relating to the renovation of the headquarters, the amounts $350,000 and…"
20. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [12:55](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-12-55) — "From this point, the procedure is similar to that already illustrated for inserting or adding."
21. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [21:7](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-21-7) — "Effect of Adjournment on Pending Business or on an Uncompleted Order of Business."
22. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [16:23](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-16-23) — "If the assembly is not familiar with the use of the Previous Question, the chair should at this point explain it."
23. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [16:27](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-16-27) — "Assume that a resolution, an amendment to the resolution, and a motion to Commit are pending (in which case the motion to Commit is the immediately pending question)."
24. Answer: **Commit**. See RONR (12th ed.) [13:9](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-13-9) — "Dilatory Motion to Commit."
25. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [16:21](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-16-21) — "In stating the question on this undebatable, unamendable motion, the chair does not pause or ask, “Are you ready for the question?” but puts the question for a rising vote on the motion for the Previous Question immediately, as shown below."
26. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [13:22](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-13-22) — "After a question has been referred to a committee and at any time before the committee submits its report, even at another session, the assembly by a majority vote can give the committee additional instructions in reference to the referred question (see also 13:8(d))."
27. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [15:17](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-15-17) — "Unlike the case of main motions and lower-ranking subsidiary motions (Postpone Indefinitely, Amend, Commit, Postpone), the adoption of one motion limiting or extending debate in a certain way does not prevent another such conflicting motion from being in order."
28. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [12:34](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-12-34) — "Therefore, when stating the question on an amendment, the chair may find it advisable to employ three steps:"
29. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [22:11](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-22-11) — "It should be noted that the adoption of this motion does not adjourn the present meeting or set a time for its adjournment; thus, it has no direct effect on when the present meeting shall adjourn, and is very different from a motion to fix the time at which to adjourn (which is always a main motion)."
30. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [12:110](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-12-110) — "On the other hand, suppose that the motion or resolution is “to sell the headquarters for an amount not less than $ .” In the case of such a motion—to accept a sum of money in settlement—the amounts being considered should be arranged and voted on in order from the smallest to the largest."
31. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [13:10](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-13-10) — "When a motion to Commit merely lacks essential details—for example, when the motion is made simply “to refer the main question to a committee”—the chair should not rule it out of order."
32. Answer: **Indefinitely**. See RONR (12th ed.) [11:3](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-11-3) — "Consequently, the adoption of the motion to Postpone Indefinitely is in effect an indirect rejection of the main motion."
33. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [12:57](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-12-57) — "To avoid confusion with the form of amendment known as Substitute (12:69–90), which applies to paragraphs or longer elements, the word substitute should not be used in connection with the motion to strike out and insert, which applies to words."
34. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [12:85](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-12-85) — "Brief debate shows that the proposed survey could not be properly carried out in twenty days."
35. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [16:13](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-16-13) — "Reconsideration of a Vote That Has Ordered the Previous Question."
36. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [14:9](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-14-9) — "Neither the motion to Postpone to a Certain Time nor any amendment to it is in order if the effect would be the same as that of the motion to Postpone Indefinitely—that is, if it would kill the measure."
37. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [12:28](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-12-28) — "After words have been inserted or added, they cannot be changed or struck out during the same session, except through a reconsideration of the vote (see 37), or through an amendment presenting a new question in the form of a motion:"
38. Answer: **aye**. See RONR (12th ed.) [12:21](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-12-21) — "Those of the opinion that the amendment is germane, say aye."
39. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [16:8](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-16-8) — "Exemption of Undebated Preamble from the Previous Question Unless Separately Ordered."
40. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [17:14](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-17-14) — "It is not in order to move to lay a pending question on the table if there is evidently no other matter requiring immediate attention."
41. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [12:91](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-12-91) — "The term “friendly amendment” is often used to describe an amendment offered by someone who is in sympathy with the purposes of the main motion, in the belief that the amendment will either improve the statement or effect of the main motion, presumably to the satisfaction of its maker, or will increase the chances of…"
42. Answer: **Postpone Indefinitely**. See RONR (12th ed.) [11:1](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-11-1) — "Postpone Indefinitely is a motion that the assembly decline to take a position on the main question."
43. Answer: **adding**. See RONR (12th ed.) [12:90](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-12-90) — "If the motion to substitute has been adopted, the resolution now pending is in the position of a paragraph that has been inserted, and it can no longer be amended during the same session except by adding nonmodifying matter."
44. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [12:75](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-12-75) — "If a motion to substitute is lost, the assembly has decided only that the paragraph proposed as a substitute shall not replace the one specified."
45. Answer: **Previous Question**. See RONR (12th ed.) [16:10](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-16-10) — "If a question or series of questions (including motions on which the Previous Question has been ordered) ceases to be the pending business before all of the motions affected by the order have been voted on, execution of the order is said to be interrupted."
46. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [22:1](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-22-1) — "The object of the motion to Fix the Time to Which to Adjourn (also referred to as the motion to “fix the time for an adjourned meeting”) is to set the time, and sometimes the place, for another meeting to continue business of the session, with no effect on when the present meeting will adjourn."
47. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [16:7](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-16-7) — "Sometimes the mere making of a motion for the Previous Question or “call for the question” may motivate unanimous consent to ending debate."
48. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [12:68](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-12-68) — "Debate on the amendment is limited to the relative advantages of the two sites."
49. Answer: **Fix the**. See RONR (12th ed.) [22:17](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-22-17) — "As a second example, assume that the motion to Fix the Time to Which to Adjourn is to be made with a view to immediate adjournment to a specified time, when this purpose cannot be reached by a main motion:"

139. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [14:13](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-14-13) — "A postponed question becomes an order of the day for the session, day, meeting, or hour to which it is postponed."
140. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [12:104](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-12-104) — "It should be noted that the vote that fills a blank does not decide the main question or other pending question that contained the blank."
141. Answer: **Postpone Indefinitely**. See RONR (12th ed.) [11:4](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-11-4) — "Effect of Referral (of the Main Motion) on a Pending Motion to Postpone Indefinitely."
142. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [17:8](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-17-8) — "A question that has been laid on the table remains there and can be taken from the table during the same session (8), or, if the next regular business session will be held before a quarterly time interval has elapsed (see 9:7), also until the end of the next regular session."
143. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [12:5](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-12-5) — "Neither the member who offers an amendment nor the maker of the main motion amends or “makes an amendment”; only the assembly can do that."
144. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [12:61](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-12-61) — "When such a primary amendment is offered, the chair states the question on it and lets debate of its merits begin in the usual way."
145. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [12:52](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-12-52) — "After a paragraph has been struck out, it cannot be inserted again unless the wording (or, possibly, the place) is changed in a way that presents an essentially new question."
146. Answer: **Call for the Orders of the Day**. See RONR (12th ed.) [14:17](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-14-17) — "however, if the chair fails to state the question at the correct time, any member may then demand that the postponed question be taken up as ordered, by making a Call for the Orders of the Day (18)."
147. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [22:19](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-22-19) — "If it is adopted, Member X, after the question has been restated on the pending bylaw amendment, again rises and addresses the chair."
148. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [22:5](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-22-5) — "The following eight characteristics apply only to the privileged motion to Fix the Time to Which to Adjourn."
149. Answer: **substitute**. See RONR (12th ed.) 150. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [14:2](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-14-2) — "At the time when a postponed question is due to come up, there may be another question pending, or other business of a higher priority than the postponed question, that would delay its consideration, as fully explained in 41."

153. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [12:49](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-12-49) — "The motion to amend by striking out certain words can be amended only by striking out words from the primary amendment."
154. Answer: **Refer**. See RONR (12th ed.) [13:1](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-13-1) — "The subsidiary motion to Commit or Refer is generally used to send a pending question to a relatively small group of selected persons—a committee—so that the question may be carefully investigated and put into better condition for the assembly to consider."
155. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [12:26](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-12-26) — "A motion to insert words must specify the exact place of insertion by naming the word before or after which, or the words between which, the insertion is to be made—whichever will better locate and point out the effect of the change."
156. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [22:20](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-22-20) — "The chair states the question on the motion to Adjourn and immediately puts it to vote."
157. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [19:10](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-19-10) — "If the motion made as a question of privilege is seconded, and if the chair admits it as such and decides that it should be entertained immediately, he states the question on it and proceeds as with any other main motion."
158. Answer: **Something Previously Adopted**. See RONR (12th ed.) [14:3](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-14-3) — "If the effect would be to change action already taken by the assembly, as, for example, “to postpone for three weeks the dinner scheduled for October 15,” such a motion is a particular case of the motion to Amend Something Previously Adopted (35)."
159. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) 160. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [12:83](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-12-83) — "Debate points strongly to a need for further investigation, but many members are determined to secure immediate authorization."
161. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [16:11](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-16-11) — "The Previous Question is said to be exhausted (in reference to a particular order for it) when all of the motions on which it was ordered have been finally disposed of, or when any motions not yet finally disposed of are no longer affected by the order."
162. Answer: **Commit**. See RONR (12th ed.) [13:8](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-13-8) — "The motion to Commit usually should include all necessary details:"

[12:76](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-12-76) — "When a question is being considered by paragraph or seriatim (28), it is in order to move a substitute for any paragraph or section at the time that the paragraph or section is opened to amendment."
164. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [15:10](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-15-10) — "If the limitation or extension that has been ordered does not provide for closing debate—for example, if the order was “that debate be limited to one speech of five minutes for each member,” as in Form and Example (a) below—it has no effect on what subsidiary motions can be made."
165. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [14:6](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-14-6) — "In a case where more than a quarterly time interval (see 9:7) will elapse between meetings (for example, in an annual convention of delegates or in a local society that holds only an annual meeting), a question cannot be postponed beyond the end of the present session."
166. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [19:11](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-19-11) — "“I rise to a question of privilege affecting [or “relating to”] the assembly” (or “to a question of the privileges of the assembly”), and “I rise to a question of personal privilege.” The preceding forms should always be adhered to in cases where it is necessary to interrupt a person speaking."
167. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [12:73](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-12-73) — "In taking the vote on whether to make the substitution, the chair should first read both the paragraph of the original text and the proposed substitute—as they stand at the time as amended."
168. Answer: **Commit**. See RONR (12th ed.) [13:14](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-13-14) — "If the motion to Commit lacks any other detail, the chair proceeds in a similar fashion to obtain completion of the motion."
169. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) 170. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [12:32](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-12-32) — "Typical forms in which a motion to insert, or to add, may be made are:"
171. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) 172. Answer: **Adjourn**. See RONR (12th ed.) [21:18](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-21-18) — "If the motion is lost, the chair, after announcing the result, immediately restates the resolution that was pending when the motion to Adjourn was made."
173. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [12:106](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-12-106) — "If no more suggestions are offered than the number required to fill the blank, then unless the voting is to be by ballot or roll call, those suggestions are deemed inserted by unanimous consent, and no vote is taken on inserting them."
174. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [14:14](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-14-14) — "Orders of the day consist of general orders and special orders."
175. Answer: **Previous Question**. See RONR (12th ed.) [16:14](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-16-14) — "If the execution of an order for the Previous Question was interrupted before any vote was taken under the order, and if the questions come up again during the same session, a motion to reconsider the order (if not made earlier) can be made only in the moment after the chair has announced these questions as the pending business and before any of them are voted on."
176. Answer: **sine die**. See RONR (12th ed.) [21:8](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-21-8) — "A motion to close the session in an assembly that will thereby be dissolved, or will not meet again for a long time unless called into authorized special session under the bylaws or other governing rule, is often referred to as a motion to “adjourn sine die,” which means to “adjourn without day” (see also 8:2(6))."
177. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [13:19](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-13-19) — "If a motion to Postpone Indefinitely is pending when the main motion is referred to a committee, the motion for indefinite postponement is dropped from further consideration."
178. Answer: **Amend**. See RONR (12th ed.) [12:69](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-12-69) — "A motion to Amend by striking out an entire paragraph, section, or article—or a complete main motion or resolution—and inserting a different paragraph or other unit in its place is called a motion to substitute, and the paragraph or resolution to be inserted is said to be offered (or proposed) as “a substitute.” A substitute can be offered for a paragraph or a main motion of only one sentence, and in such a case the paragraph proposed as a substitute can contain several sentences."
179. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [12:111](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-12-111) — "When a blank is to be filled with a place, date, or number, a choice of methods for arranging and voting on the proposals can be made as follows:"

182. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [15:2](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-15-2) — "The motion to Limit or Extend Limits of Debate can limit debate by:"

185. Answer: **Lay on the Table**. See RONR (12th ed.) [17:13](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-17-13) — "As stated at the beginning of this section, the motion to Lay on the Table is subject to a number of incorrect uses that must be avoided."
186. Answer: **Previous**. See RONR (12th ed.) [16:19](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-16-19) — "The general rules as to the effect of an unexhausted order for the Previous Question on subsequent motions that would normally be debatable or amendable are as follows:"

188. Answer: **Suspend the Rules**. See RONR (12th ed.) [17:10](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-17-10) — "Taking up the desired business may require an additional motion after the question has been laid on the table (see Suspend the Rules, 25;"
189. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [12:84](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-12-84) — "The chair states the question on this amendment, making its effect clear, and, after debate, puts it to vote."

## Domain 3: Incidental Motions and Motions that Bring a Question Again Before the Assembly

**1.** _Quote → section (MCQ)_ — From which section of RONR (12th ed.) is the following?

   "A request to be excused from a duty essential to the functioning of a society or assembly is a question of privilege affecting the organization of the assembly; and so also is the filling of a vacancy created by the acceptance of a resignation."

   A. 12:70
   B. 56:14
   C. 32:7
   D. 36:15

**2.** _Stated in section (MCQ)_ — Which of the following statements appears in RONR (12th ed.) 33:13?

   A. When the amounts involved are very large and the reports complicated, or the organization’s contributors or others require it, it is desirable to have the audits made by independent certified accountants.
   B. After a motion has been stated by the chair, it belongs to the meeting as a whole, and the maker must request the assembly’s permission to withdraw or modify his own motion, according to the rules stated in Standard Characteristics 1–8, above.
   C. In a separate section it should be provided that “The regular meeting… [specifying which one, as “on the last Tuesday in May”] shall be known as the annual meeting.” As explained in 9, this meeting is conducted in the same way as any regular meeting, except that officers are elected and annual reports are received…
   D. Even in a small meeting, the presiding officer of an assembly is not addressed or referred to by name.

**3.** _Quote → section (MCQ)_ — From which section of RONR (12th ed.) is the following?

   "A question that has been laid on the table remains there and can be taken from the table during the same session (8), or, if the next regular business session will be held before a quarterly time interval has elapsed (see 9:7), also until the end of the next regular session."

   A. 43:15
   B. 62:15
   C. 19:8
   D. 34:3

**4.** _Quote → section (MCQ)_ — From which section of RONR (12th ed.) is the following?

   "If any member objects, a member has no right to read from—or to have the secretary read from—any paper or book as a part of his speech without permission of the assembly."

   A. 59:62
   B. 33:20
   C. 2:21
   D. 56:39

**5.** _Stated in section (MCQ)_ — Which of the following statements appears in RONR (12th ed.) 31:7?

   A. (For more complete explanations of the general forms observed by the presiding officer and members in an assembly, see 42 and 43.)
   B. A resolution or a long or complicated motion should be prepared in advance of the meeting, if possible, and should be put into writing before it is offered.
   C. The time at which nominations shall be closed or reopened can be specified in the motion, or added by amendment.
   D. A Report on a Resolution Previously Referred to a Committee.

**6.** _Quote → section (MCQ)_ — From which section of RONR (12th ed.) is the following?

   "When a motion to Reconsider covers the votes on two or more connected motions, not all of these questions can be discussed in debate on the motion to Reconsider, but only the one that will be voted on first if the motion to Reconsider is adopted."

   A. 37:32
   B. 45:68
   C. 47:48
   D. 56:17

**7.** _Quote → section (MCQ)_ — From which section of RONR (12th ed.) is the following?

   "The object of motions relating to methods of voting and the polls is to obtain a vote on a question in some form other than by voice, by show of hands, or by Division (rising); or to otherwise direct how and when voting is to be conducted."

   A. 4:15
   B. 41:70
   C. 30:1
   D. 14:13

   A. At the end of the specified time, the chair gains the attention of the assembly and begins:
   B. Motions relating to opening and closing the polls are applicable only with respect to ballot votes.
   C. For a member to begin to discuss a matter while no question is pending, without promptly leading to a motion, implies an unusual circumstance and requires permission of the assembly (see 33:22) in addition to obtaining the floor.
   D. In putting the question to a vote, the chair may initially omit reading the proposed rules.

   D. As noted in Standard Descriptive Characteristic 6 above, when previous notice is a requirement for the adoption of a motion to Rescind or Amend Something Previously Adopted, no subsidiary motion to Amend is in order that proposes a change greater than that for which notice was given.

   C. The time at which the polls shall be closed or reopened can be specified in the motion, or added by amendment.
   D. If the offense is more serious than in the case above—as when a member repeatedly questions the motives of other members whom he mentions by name, or persists in speaking on completely irrelevant matters in debate—the chair normally should first warn the member; but with or without such a warning, the chair or any…

**21.** _Cloze recall_ — Fill in the blank: After a motion to _____ and Enter on the Minutes has been called up, its treatment is the same as that of the regular motion to Reconsider.

**22.** _Stated in section (MCQ)_ — Which of the following statements appears in RONR (12th ed.) 30:10?

   A. If members enter afterward and it is desired to reopen the polls, this can be done by a majority vote.
   B. If a motion to strike out certain words is adopted, the same words cannot be inserted again during the same session unless the place or the wording is so changed as to make a new proposition.
   C. Any person at a mass meeting who, after being advised, persists in an obvious attempt to divert the meeting to a different purpose from that for which it was called, or who otherwise tries to disrupt the proceedings, becomes subject to the disciplinary procedures described in 61.
   D. Before a member in an assembly can make a motion or speak in debate—the parliamentary name given to any form of discussion of the merits of a motion—he must obtain the floor; that is, he must be recognized by the chair as having the exclusive right to be heard at that time.

**23.** _Cloze recall_ — Fill in the blank: By means of the motion to _____ from further consideration of a question or subject, the assembly can take the matter out of a committee’s hands after referring it to the committee and before the committee has made a final report on it, and the assembly itself can consider it.

In the foregoing connection, it should be noted that under parliamentary conditions the inclusion of supporting facts or reasoning in a report proposing certain action may tend to work against the taking of that action, since some members who might otherwise have been willing to accept the proposals may be led to vote…
   C. If, in unfolding the ballots, it is found that two or more filledout ballots are folded together, they are recorded as illegal votes—that is, each set of ballots folded together is reported as one illegal vote, and is not credited.
   D. In societies having very frequent regular meetings primarily for presentation of a program, and also monthly or quarterly business meetings (9:1), it is well to permit action on amendments to the bylaws only at a quarterly or annual meeting or their adjournments.

   "When it is moved to reconsider a debatable subsidiary or incidental motion which relates to a pending main question or a series of pending questions (in which case the motion to Reconsider is debatable, as noted in Standard Characteristic 5), debate on the motion to Reconsider can go into the merits of the motion…"

   A. 40:3
   B. 4:16
   C. 51:46
   D. 37:29

**143.** _Cloze recall_ — Fill in the blank: To provide both usefulness and protection against abuse, the motion to Reconsider has the following unique _____, as more fully explained in 37:10:

**Answer Key**

1. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [32:7](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-32-7) — "A request to be excused from a duty essential to the functioning of a society or assembly is a question of privilege affecting the organization of the assembly; and so also is the filling of a vacancy created by the acceptance of a resignation."
2. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [33:13](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-33-13) — "After a motion has been stated by the chair, it belongs to the meeting as a whole, and the maker must request the assembly’s permission to withdraw or modify his own motion, according to the rules stated in Standard Characteristics 1–8, above."
3. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [34:3](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-34-3) — "A question that has been laid on the table remains there and can be taken from the table during the same session (8), or, if the next regular business session will be held before a quarterly time interval has elapsed (see 9:7), also until the end of the next regular session."
4. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [33:20](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-33-20) — "If any member objects, a member has no right to read from—or to have the secretary read from—any paper or book as a part of his speech without permission of the assembly."
5. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [31:7](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-31-7) — "The time at which nominations shall be closed or reopened can be specified in the motion, or added by amendment."
6. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [37:32](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-37-32) — "When a motion to Reconsider covers the votes on two or more connected motions, not all of these questions can be discussed in debate on the motion to Reconsider, but only the one that will be voted on first if the motion to Reconsider is adopted."
7. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [30:1](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-30-1) — "The object of motions relating to methods of voting and the polls is to obtain a vote on a question in some form other than by voice, by show of hands, or by Division (rising); or to otherwise direct how and when voting is to be conducted."
8. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [30:8](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-30-8) — "Motions relating to opening and closing the polls are applicable only with respect to ballot votes."
9. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [25:11](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-25-11) — "Rules protecting a basic right of the individual member cannot be suspended."

12. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) If a member commits only a slight breach of order—such as addressing another member instead of the chair in debate, or, in a single instance, failing to confine his remarks to the merits of the pending question—the chair simply raps lightly, points out the fault, and advises the member to avoid it.
   C. For certain limited purposes not involving debate or amendment—such as to make a privileged motion or a motion to Reconsider (37)—a member can claim the floor while the motion to Lay on the Table is pending.
   D. If the existence of an error or material omission in the minutes becomes reasonably established after their approval —even many years later—the minutes can then be corrected by means of the motion to Amend Something Previously Adopted (35), which requires a two-thirds vote, or a majority vote with notice, or the vote…

The basic principle of decision in a deliberative assembly is that, to become the act or choice of the body, a proposition must be adopted by a majority vote; that is, direct approval— implying assumption of responsibility for the act—must be registered by more than half of the members present and voting on the…

**282.** _Quote → section (MCQ)_ — From which section of RONR (12th ed.) is the following?

   "Either the chair on his own initiative or the assembly by a majority vote can order such a vote to be counted."

   A. 1:9
   B. 13:2
   C. 4:53
   D. 41:69

**Answer Key**

1. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [41:63](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-41-63) — "When the adoption of a proposed agenda is pending, it is subject to amendment by majority vote."
2. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [48:6](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-48-6) — "The use by the secretary of a recording device can be of great benefit in preparing the minutes, but a transcription from it should never be used as the minutes themselves."
3. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [43:34](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-43-34) — "In general, for a member to speak when no question is pending, without promptly leading to a motion, implies an unusual circumstance and requires permission of the assembly."
4. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [43:31](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-43-31) — "Allowable Explanations and Requests When No Motion Is Pending or When an Undebatable Motion Is Pending."
5. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [47:29](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-47-29) — "Some societies elect several vice-presidents in an order of precedence—first, second, third, and so on—in which case the highest-ranking one present has the duty of serving in place of the president when needed."
6. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [4:10](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-4-10) — "If no member seconds the motion, the chair must be sure that all have heard it before proceeding to other business."
7. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [2:21](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-2-21) — "Rules of order—whether contained in the parliamentary authority or adopted as special rules of order—can be suspended by a two-thirds vote as explained in 25 (with the exceptions there specified)."
8. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [9:14](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-9-14) — "Special meetings can properly be called only (a) as authorized in the bylaws (see 56:36); or (b) when authorized by the assembly itself, as part of formal disciplinary procedures, for purposes of conducting a trial and determining a punishment (see 63:21n9)."
9. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [43:30](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-43-30) — "In debate on an appeal (24) or a point of order that the chair has submitted to the judgment of the assembly (23:18– 21), the foregoing rule does not apply, and the presiding officer does not leave the chair, since his participation in the debate relates to the function of presiding."
10. Answer: **Pattern of Formality**. See RONR (12th ed.) [43:19](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-43-19) — "Paragraphs 3:9–13 under the head Pattern of Formality should be read in connection with this subject."
11. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [2:17](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-2-17) — "Special rules of order are usually adopted in the form of resolutions (4:4–5, 10:13–23), but when they are printed, the enacting words (such as “Resolved, That”) are normally dropped."
12. Answer: **Request for**. See RONR (12th ed.) [43:22](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-43-22) — "If, while a member is speaking in debate, another member wishes to address a question to him—which the person speaking can permit or not as he chooses, but which is taken out of his time if he does— the member desiring to ask the question rises and addresses the chair, proceeding as explained under Request for Information (33:6–10)."
13. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [47:18](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-47-18) — "When a vote is taken, the result should be announced and also what question, if any, is then pending, before any member who addresses the chair is recognized."
14. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [47:24](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-47-24) — "When a vice-president is presiding over the assembly, he or she is addressed as “Mr."
15. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [41:64](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-41-64) — "In reference to an order of business specially adopted for a given session, the term program is often used instead of agenda; but while the latter technically includes only items of business, the former may include also the times for speakers, meals, and other nonbusiness matters."
16. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [41:49](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-41-49) — "Rules of precedence affecting general orders for particular hours."
17. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [4:45](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-4-45) — "Form of announcement of voting result and the business that follows."
18. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [4:4](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-4-4) — "To make a main motion, a member must obtain the floor, as explained above, when no other question is pending and when business of the kind represented by the motion is in order."
19. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [41:20](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-41-20) — "Matters that the bylaws require to be considered at a particular meeting, such as the nomination and election of officers, may be regarded as special orders for the meeting and be considered under the heading of Special Orders in the order of business."
20. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [41:68](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-41-68) — "In the case of a recess, any pending business is interrupted for the recess, and taken up again after the recess."
21. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [42:15](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-42-15) — "If at any time the chair makes a mistake and assigns the floor to the wrong person when more than one member rose and addressed the chair promptly, a Point of Order can be raised."
22. Answer: **parliamentary law**. See RONR (12th ed.) [1:5](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-1-5) — "A deliberative assembly that has not adopted any rules is commonly understood to hold itself bound by the rules and customs of the general parliamentary law—or common parliamentary law (as discussed in the Introduction)—to the extent that there is agreement in the meeting body as to what these rules and practices are."
23. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [41:7](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-41-7) — "The presiding officer may find it helpful to have at hand a memorandum of the complete order of business, listing, under headings (2) and (3) as explained below, all known reports which are expected to be presented, and under headings (4) and (5), all matters which the minutes show are due to come up, arranged in…"
24. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [9:33](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-9-33) — "Various provisions for electronic meetings are possible, so that more than the minimum standard of an audioconference may be required."
25. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [8:13](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-8-13) — "Relation of a Session’s Freedom to the Rules of an Organization."
26. Answer: **any**. See RONR (12th ed.) [43:5](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-43-5) — "A member may both speak in debate and conclude by offering a secondary motion, which is a particular application of the principle that a member having been recognized for any legitimate purpose has the floor for all legitimate purposes."
27. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [43:15](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-43-15) — "The rule allowing each member two speeches of ten minutes’ length per day on each debatable question can be made either more restrictive or more liberal for all meetings of a society by adopting a special rule of order by a two-thirds vote after notice, or by a vote of a majority of the entire membership (2:14ff.; see…"
28. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [43:28](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-43-28) — "During debate, during remarks by the presiding officer to the assembly, and during voting, no member should be permitted to disturb the assembly by whispering, walking across the floor, or in any other way."
29. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [3:28](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-3-28) — "The reading of a communication does not in itself formally bring a question before the assembly."
30. Answer: **unfinished business,**. See RONR (12th ed.) [41:21](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-41-21) — "The term unfinished business, in cases where the regular business meetings of an organization are not separated by more than a quarterly time interval (9:7), refers to questions that have come over from the previous meeting (other than special orders) as a result of that meeting’s having adjourned without completing its order of business (21:7(b)) and without scheduling an adjourned meeting (9, 22) to complete it."
31. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [41:25](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-41-25) — "Any item of business (in whatever class) that is on the table can be taken from the table under this heading at any time when no question is pending (17, 34)."
32. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [9:16](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-9-16) — "The requirement that business transacted at a special meeting be specified in the call should not be confused with a requirement that previous notice of a motion be given."
33. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [3:18](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-3-18) — "A mass meeting usually requires no order of business, since, referring to the headings listed above, there is nothing but new business to be brought up (unless the meeting is one within a series)."
34. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [47:20](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-47-20) — "All of the duties of the presiding officer described above relate to the function of presiding over the assembly at its meetings."
35. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [5:11](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-5-11) — "Viewed apart from incidental motions and with modifications under particular conditions explained in 6:7, the main motion, the seven subsidiary motions, and the five privileged motions fall into a definite order of precedence, which gives a particular rank to each of these thirteen motions."
36. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [4:43](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-4-43) — "In general (that is, as applying to main motions and other types of motions explained in later chapters), the chair’s announcement of the result of the vote includes the following:"
37. Answer: **class**. See RONR (12th ed.) [41:38](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-41-38) — "It is not in order to lay on the table or postpone a class of questions, like committee reports, or anything but the question that is actually before the assembly."
38. Answer: **expressly**. See RONR (12th ed.) [47:28](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-47-28) — "In case of the president’s resignation, death, or removal, the vice-president automatically becomes president for the remainder of the term, unless the bylaws expressly provide otherwise for filling a vacancy in the office of president (see also 56:32)."
39. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [42:22](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-42-22) — "When a member has risen to claim the floor or has been assigned the floor, it is out of order for another to call out a motion to adjourn, or a motion to lay the pending question on the table."
40. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [41:44](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-41-44) — "When a question that is not pending is made an order of the day, it is usually made a special order."
41. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [47:5](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-47-5) — "The presiding officer of an assembly ordinarily is called the chairman when no special title has been assigned, or in a body not permanently organized, such as a mass meeting (53)."
42. Answer: **Reconsider**. See RONR (12th ed.) [42:12](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-42-12) — "When an undebatable motion that can be amended is reconsidered for that announced purpose, however, the maker of the motion to Reconsider (37) is entitled to preference in recognition, as explained in the preceding paragraph."
43. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [40:4](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-40-4) — "Note on Procedure in Changing the Quorum Provision in Bylaws."
44. Answer: **receive**. See RONR (12th ed.) [3:27](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-3-27) — "It is not customary to make a motion to receive a communication or a committee report, which means only to permit or cause such a paper to be read."
45. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [3:29](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-3-29) — "Business That Comes Up Without a Motion, Because of Previous Action."
46. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [48:26](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-48-26) — "If the treasurer presents an unaudited annual report or other financial report that the bylaws require to be audited, and if there is a standing auditing committee or if auditors have already been chosen in some other manner, the chair, without waiting for a motion when the treasurer has finished reading his report,…"
47. Answer: **standing rule of**. See RONR (12th ed.) [43:16](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-43-16) — "In a convention—where the limits of debate generally need to be stricter than in a local society—such a modification is usually adopted in the form of a standing rule of the convention (59), requiring a two-thirds vote in such a case."
48. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [4:24](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-4-24) — "Before the question is stated no debate may accompany suggestions that a motion be modified or withdrawn."
49. Answer: **the**. See RONR (12th ed.) [41:12](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-41-12) — "The secretary’s draft of the minutes is often sent to all members in advance of the meeting at which those minutes are to be approved, usually with the meeting notice."
50. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [41:34](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-41-34) — "This heading, included by some types of societies in their order of business, refers to the general welfare of the organization, and may vary in character."
51. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [43:24](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-43-24) — "Refraining from Speaking Adversely on a Prior Action Not Pending."
52. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [43:2](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-43-2) — "Debatability is a characteristic of all main motions and of certain other motions, depending on the parliamentary function they serve, according to principles summarized at the end of this section; and from such principles are derived the specific rules stated under Standard Characteristic 5 in 11–37."
53. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [41:31](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-41-31) — "In some organizations it is customary at meetings to call the roll of officers in order to verify their attendance—or, sometimes in very small societies, even to call the roll of members."
54. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [43:21](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-43-21) — "When a question is pending, a member can condemn the nature or likely consequences of the proposed measure in strong terms, but he must avoid personalities, and under no circumstances can he attack or question the motives of another member."
55. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [41:39](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-41-39) — "The chair himself cannot depart from the prescribed order of business, which only the assembly can do by at least a twothirds vote."
56. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [9:29](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-9-29) — "In meetings of many public bodies, such as school boards, the public may attend."
57. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [41:10](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-41-10) — "A formal motion to approve the minutes is not necessary, although such a motion is not out of order."
58. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [39:4](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-39-4) — "It is the duty of the presiding officer to prevent members from misusing the legitimate forms of motions, or abusing the privilege of renewing certain motions, merely to obstruct business."
59. Answer: **legislative body**. See RONR (12th ed.) [1:19](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-1-19) — "The term legislative body refers to a constitutionally established public lawmaking body of representatives chosen by the electorate for a fixed term of office—such as Congress or a state legislature."
60. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [41:30](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-41-30) — "Opening ceremonies immediately after the meeting is called to order may include the invocation (which, if offered, should always be placed first), the singing of the national anthem, the reciting of the Pledge of Allegiance to the flag, a ritual briefly recalling the objects or ideals of the organization, or the like."
61. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [43:17](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-43-17) — "While a debatable question is immediately pending, the allowed length or number of speeches can be reduced or increased, for that question only, by means of the subsidiary motion to Limit or Extend Limits of Debate (15), adopted by a two-thirds vote."
62. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [5:7](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-5-7) — "When a secondary motion is placed before the assembly, it becomes the immediately pending question; the main motion remains pending while the secondary motion is also pending."
63. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [9:36](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-9-36) — "If an organization authorizes its assembly, boards, or committees to hold electronic meetings, such a provision should indicate whether members who are not present in person have the right to participate by electronic means, or whether the body may choose to allow or disallow such participation; and, conversely,…"
64. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [4:58](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-4-58) — "In cases where there seems to be no opposition in routine business or on questions of little importance, time can often be saved by the procedure of unanimous consent, or as it was formerly also called, general consent."
65. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [47:43](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-47-43) — "The term executive secretary, or executive director, is usually applied to a salaried officer who devotes full time to the position of administrative officer and general manager of an organization, especially at the national, regional, or state level; and unless otherwise indicated the term is used in that sense in…"
66. Answer: **majority**. See RONR (12th ed.) [1:7](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-1-7) — "When a decision is to be based on more than a majority, the requirement most commonly specified is a two-thirds vote— that is, the expressed approval of at least two thirds of those present and voting."

246. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [41:67](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-41-67) — "When the chair announces the hour, any member can move to reschedule the time for recess or adjournment, or to extend the time of considering the pending question for a specified period."
247. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) 261. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [43:26](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-43-26) — "Reading from Reports, Quotations, etc., Only Without Objection or With Permission."

264. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [4:54](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-4-54) — "(For additional information regarding Division of the Assembly and motions relating to voting, see 29 and 30.)"

266. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [9:5](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-9-5) — "When notice is required to be sent, unless a different standard is specified that requirement is met if written notice is sent to each member either:"
267. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [4:30](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-4-30) — "Debate must be confined to the merits of the pending question."

272. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) 273. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [43:23](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-43-23) — "As much as possible, the use of names of members should be avoided in debate."

275. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) 276. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [1:8](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-1-8) — "Whenever the rules of an assembly require a majority vote, a two-thirds vote, or any other basis for decision, it must be understood that, unless otherwise specified in the rules (as in the case of certain procedural actions), such a vote is effective only if taken when the necessary minimum number of members, known…"
277. Answer: **Point of Order**. See RONR (12th ed.) [2:25](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-2-25) — "However, if a customary practice is or becomes in conflict with the parliamentary authority or any written rule, and a Point of Order (23) citing the conflict is raised at any time, the custom falls to the ground, and the conflicting provision in the parliamentary authority or written rule must thereafter be complied with."
278. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [2:15](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-2-15) — "In contrast to bylaws, rules of order derive their proper substance largely from the general nature of the parliamentary process rather than from the circumstances of a particular assembly."
279. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) 280. Answer: **Form and Example**. See RONR (12th ed.) [4:48](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-4-48) — "The full sequence of announcing the voting result and the business that follows is frequently illustrated in the subsections Form and Example in the sections covering the different parliamentary motions in chapters VI–IX, and in 10:38–43 as applied to the main motion."
281. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [5:1](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-5-1) — "As noted in Chapter II, the word motion refers to a formal proposal by a member, in a meeting, that the assembly take certain action."
282. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [4:53](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-4-53) — "Either the chair on his own initiative or the assembly by a majority vote can order such a vote to be counted."

## Domain 5: Voting, Nominations, and Elections

**1.** _Stated in section (MCQ)_ — Which of the following statements appears in RONR (12th ed.) 46:48?

   A. The privileged motion to Adjourn (which is always moved in an unqualified form with no mention of a time either for adjourning or for meeting again) is a motion to close the meeting immediately, made under conditions where some other provision for another meeting exists (so that the adjournment will not have the…
   B. Depending on the circumstances, the voting body may be able to order a recount if an election was conducted by ballot (see 45:41), roll-call vote (see 45:54), or counted vote (see the last sentence of 45:15).
   C. If no member of the temporary minority voted on the prevailing side and it is too late for anyone to change his vote (see 45:9), notice can be given that a motion to rescind the assembly’s action will be made at the next meeting.
   D. Punishments that a society can impose generally fall under the headings of censure, fine (if authorized in the bylaws), suspension, or expulsion.

   A. Remedy When Action Taken by an Executive Board Is Null and Void.
   B. A two-thirds vote—when the term is unqualified—means at least two thirds of the votes cast by persons entitled to vote, excluding blanks or abstentions, at a regular or properly called meeting.
   C. Although the program must come before the convention for adoption and can be amended by it, many details must be decided far ahead.
   D. An Objection to the Consideration of a Question is similar in some ways to a Point of Order.

   C. In preparing bylaws and interpreting them, the following principles of interpretation—which have equal application to other rules and documents adopted by an organization—may be of assistance.
   D. A proxy is a power of attorney given by one person to another to vote in his stead; the term also designates the person who holds the power of attorney.
