**72.** _Quote → section (MCQ)_ — From which section of RONR (12th ed.) is the following?

   "Because the voting body itself is the ultimate judge of election disputes, only that body has the authority to resolve them in the absence of a bylaw or special rule of order that specifically grants another body that authority."

   A. 49:4
   B. 59:51
   C. 46:50
   D. 45:54

**Answer Key**

1. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [46:48](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-46-48) — "Depending on the circumstances, the voting body may be able to order a recount if an election was conducted by ballot (see 45:41), roll-call vote (see 45:54), or counted vote (see the last sentence of 45:15)."
2. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [44:3](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-44-3) — "A two-thirds vote—when the term is unqualified—means at least two thirds of the votes cast by persons entitled to vote, excluding blanks or abstentions, at a regular or properly called meeting."
3. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:18](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-18) — "Voting by ballot (also known as secret ballot) is used when secrecy of the members’ votes is desired."
4. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:41](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-41) — "After completion of an election or balloting on a motion, unless the voting body adopts an incidental main motion directing otherwise, the tellers place the ballots and tally sheets in the custody of the secretary, who keeps them under seal until the time within which a recount may be ordered expires, and then…"
5. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:14](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-14) — "In connection with the methods of voting by voice, by rising, or by show of hands, as explained in Chapter II, if the chair is in doubt on a voice vote or a vote by show of hands, he should retake it as a rising vote and, if necessary to satisfy himself of the result, he should obtain a count of it."
6. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:8](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-8) — "Except when the vote has been taken by ballot (or some other method that provides secrecy), a member has a right to change his vote up to the time the result is announced but afterward can make the change only by the unanimous consent of the assembly requested and granted, without debate, immediately following the…"
7. Answer: **unanimous consent**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:12](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-12) — "Also described in Chapter II is the procedure of action by unanimous consent."
8. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:63](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-63) — "On the preferential ballot —for each office to be filled or multiple-choice question to be decided—the voter is asked to indicate the order in which he prefers all the candidates or propositions, placing the numeral 1 beside his first preference, the numeral 2 beside his second preference, and so on for every possible…"
9. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:32](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-32) — "All ballots that indicate a preference—provided they have been cast by persons entitled to vote—are taken into account in determining the number of votes cast for purposes of computing the majority."
10. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [44:10](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-44-10) — "Whenever it is desired that the basis for decision be other than a majority vote or (where the normal rules of parliamentary law require it) a two-thirds vote or a vote of a majority of the entire membership, the desired basis should be precisely defined in the bylaws or in a special rule of order."
11. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:24](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-24) — "A ballot can consist of simply a small slip of paper on which the voter writes his choice in a manner directed by the chair; but if it is known ahead of time that a vote is to be by ballot and what the exact questions are, the ballots should be prepared in advance for distribution at the proper time."
12. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [46:26](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-46-26) — "The bylaws may provide that a member shall be a nominee upon the petition of a specified number of members."
13. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [44:1](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-44-1) — "As stated in 1:6, the basic requirement for approval of an action or choice by a deliberative assembly, except where a rule provides otherwise, is a majority vote."
14. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [46:22](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-46-22) — "The object of a nominating ballot is to provide the members with an indication of the sentiments of the voting body, which they may take into account in voting in the election."
15. Answer: **plurality vote**. See RONR (12th ed.) [44:11](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-44-11) — "A plurality vote is the largest number of votes to be given any candidate or proposition when three or more choices are possible;"
16. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:31](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-31) — "In recording the votes cast, the principle followed is that a choice has no mandate from the voting body unless approval is expressed by more than half of those entitled to vote and registering any evidence of having some preference."
17. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [46:35](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-46-35) — "If the bylaws require the election of officers to be by ballot and there is only one nominee for an office, the ballot must nevertheless be taken for that office unless the bylaws provide for an exception in such a case."
18. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:4](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-4) — "Abstaining from Voting on a Question of Direct Personal Interest."
19. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:70](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-70) — "A proxy is a power of attorney given by one person to another to vote in his stead; the term also designates the person who holds the power of attorney."
20. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [46:47](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-46-47) — "An officer-elect takes possession of his office immediately upon his election’s becoming final, unless the bylaws or other rules specify a later time (see 56:27)."
21. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [46:36](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-46-36) — "An election by ballot can be conducted by mail if the bylaws so provide, as explained in 45:57–69."
22. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [46:38](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-46-38) — "When there is more than one nominee for a given office in a viva-voce election—or in an election by rising vote or by show of hands—the candidates are voted on in the order in which they were nominated."
23. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:34](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-34) — "If, in unfolding the ballots, it is found that two or more filledout ballots are folded together, they are recorded as illegal votes—that is, each set of ballots folded together is reported as one illegal vote, and is not credited."
24. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:15](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-15) — "In small meetings, the chair can take such a count himself—with or without directing the secretary to make an independent count for verification."
25. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [44:6](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-44-6) — "The chair can obtain a count of the vote initially if it appears —when those in the affirmative rise—that the result will be close; or he can retake it as a counted rising vote if he is afterward in doubt."
26. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:29](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-29) — "When the balloting is completed, the chair directs the tellers to collect the ballots."
27. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [46:31](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-46-31) — "for election by ballot can be generally followed, and the member (or the chairman of a delegation, as the case may be), when called upon, declares his vote or the votes of the members of his delegation for each office to be filled."
28. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [46:13](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-46-13) — "It is desirable policy for the nominating committee, before making its report, to contact each person whom it wishes to nominate, in order to obtain his acceptance of nomination— that is, his assurance that he will serve in the specified office if elected."
29. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:36](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-36) — "On a ballot containing several questions or several independent offices or positions to be filled, each section of the ballot—that is, each portion that contains one question or position to be filled, or one group of identical positions (such as on a board or committee) to be filled—is treated for all purposes as if…"
30. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:48](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-48) — "The roll is called in alphabetical order except that the presiding officer’s name is called last, and only when his vote will affect the result."
31. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [46:42](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-46-42) — "Although unusual, an election can be held by roll call."
32. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:47](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-47) — "When a vote is to be taken by roll call (see 30 for the motion), the chair puts the question in a form like the following:"
33. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:62](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-62) — "The term preferential voting refers to any of a number of voting methods by which, on a single ballot when there are more than two possible choices, the second or less-preferred choices of voters can be taken into account if no candidate or proposition attains a majority."
34. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:49](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-49) — "The secretary repeats each member’s name and answer aloud as it is given and notes the answers to the roll call in separate columns."
35. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [46:9](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-46-9) — "In the election of officers of an ordinary society, nominations often are made by a nominating committee."
36. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [46:45](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-46-45) — "If, for any reason, the assembly does not complete an election at the time for which it was scheduled, it should do so as soon as possible and may do so at any time until the expiration of the term the election is to fill."
37. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:59](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-59) — "If the vote is not to be secret, the following items should be sent to each qualified voter:"
38. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [46:11](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-46-11) — "Although it is not common for the nominating committee to nominate more than one candidate for any office, the committee can do so unless the bylaws prohibit it."
39. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [46:31](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-46-31) — "Two alternative procedures for the sequence of nominating and voting in elections by ballot can be prescribed or adopted, as mentioned above."
40. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:23](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-23) — "Unless another method is specified by an appropriate rule or motion (see 45:42–43 regarding electronic or machine voting), a ballot vote is taken on slips of paper on which the voters mark their votes and is subject to the rules below."
41. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:20](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-20) — "When the bylaws require a vote to be taken by ballot, this requirement cannot be suspended—even by a unanimous vote—so as to take the vote by a nonsecret method."
42. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [46:27](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-46-27) — "In large conventions, nominations are sometimes accompanied by a speech advocating the nominee’s election."
43. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:40](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-40) — "The tellers’ report is entered in full in the minutes, becoming a part of the official records of the organization."
44. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [44:9](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-44-9) — "Regarding these bases for determining a voting result, the following points should be noted:"
45. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [46:18](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-46-18) — "After the nominating committee has presented its report and before voting for the different offices takes place, the chair must call for further nominations from the floor."
46. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:58](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-58) — "For a vote by mail—so that there may be no question of the result in the event that the vote is close—it is important that the mailing list used exactly correspond to the current official roll of voting members."
47. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [44:12](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-44-12) — "If the presiding officer is a member of the assembly, he can vote as any other member when the vote is by ballot (see also 45:28)."
48. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:3](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-3) — "Although it is the duty of every member who has an opinion on a question to express it by his vote, he can abstain, since he cannot be compelled to vote."
49. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [46:37](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-46-37) — "The viva-voce method of election finds application principally in mass meetings—or when an election is not strongly contested and the bylaws do not require election by ballot."
50. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:30](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-30) — "After all have voted who wish to, the polls can be closed on the motion of a member by a two-thirds vote (30); but it is usually best to rely on the chair to close the polls."
51. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:60](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-60) — "If the vote is to be secret, an inner return envelope—with a space for the voter’s signature placed on its face instead of on the ballot—should be sent to the voter with the ballot, in addition to the self-addressed outer return envelope described above."
52. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [46:39](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-46-39) — "It will be seen that, under the procedure just described, it is necessary for members wishing to vote for a later nominee to vote against an earlier one."
53. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:26](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-26) — "In balloting in a meeting where the voting is in the same room as the meeting, the chair appoints tellers to distribute, collect, and count the ballots, and to report the vote."
54. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [46:5](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-46-5) — "At a mass meeting it is a common practice to have the chairman nominated by the person who was designated to call the meeting to order, but an organized society should adopt other methods of nominating for office."
55. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:45](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-45) — "Taking a vote by roll call (or by yeas and nays, as it is also called) has the effect of placing on the record how each member, or sometimes each delegation, votes; therefore, it has exactly the opposite effect of a ballot vote."
56. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:56](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-56) — "It is a fundamental principle of parliamentary law that the right to vote is limited to the members of an organization who are actually present at the time the vote is taken in a regular or properly called meeting, although it should be noted that a member need not be present when the question is put."
57. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:52](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-52) — "In roll-call voting, a record of how each member voted, as well as the result of the vote, is entered in full in the journal or minutes."
58. Answer: **Postpone Indefinitely**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:21](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-21) — "Applications of this rule arise with regard to voting on motions to Postpone Indefinitely (30:5) and the reconsideration of motions that have been previously voted on by ballot (30:7)."
59. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:39](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-39) — "The tellers’ report does not include the number of members eligible to vote nor the number abstaining."
60. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [46:8](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-46-8) — "If there is no nominating committee and nominations are to be from the floor, the chair calls for them by saying, for example, “Nominations are now in order for the office of President.” If there is a nominating committee, the chair calls for nominations as shown in 46:19."
61. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [46:12](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-46-12) — "Members of the nominating committee are not barred from becoming nominees for office themselves."
62. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:1](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-1) — "A member of a society who is in arrears in payment of his dues, but who has not been formally dropped from the membership rolls and is not under a disciplinary suspension, retains the full rights of a voting member and is entitled to vote except as the bylaws may otherwise provide."
63. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:71](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-71) — "If the law under which an organization is incorporated allows proxy voting to be prohibited by a provision of the bylaws, the adoption of this book as parliamentary authority by prescription in the bylaws should be treated as sufficient provision to accomplish that result (cf. 56:49n1)."
64. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:51](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-51) — "The secretary gives the final number of those voting on each side, and the number answering present, to the chair, who announces these figures and declares the result."
65. Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:10](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-10) — "The assembly itself is the judge of all questions arising that are incidental to the voting or the counting of the votes."
66. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [44:4](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-44-4) — "As a compromise between the rights of the individual and the rights of the assembly, the principle has been established that a two-thirds vote is required to adopt any motion that:"
67. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [46:32](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-46-32) — "Whichever one of the preceding methods of election is used, if any office remains unfilled after the first ballot, the balloting is repeated for that office as many times as necessary to obtain a majority vote for a single candidate."
68. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [46:7](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-46-7) — "The same person can be nominated for more than one office, even if voting for all offices is to take place at the same time on a single ballot."
69. Answer: **aye,**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:13](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-13) — "A characteristic that the three methods of voting listed above have in common is that in each case the chair calls first for those voting in the affirmative to indicate the fact in a specified manner (“say aye,” “rise,” or “raise the right hand”), after which he calls for the negative vote, then judges and declares which side prevails."
70. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:9](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-9) — "Time Limits on Efforts to Challenge, Retake, or Change a Vote."
71. Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [45:50](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-45-50) — "At the conclusion of the roll call, the names of those who failed to answer can be called again, or the chair can ask if anyone entered the room after his or her name was called."
72. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [46:50](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-46-50) — "Because the voting body itself is the ultimate judge of election disputes, only that body has the authority to resolve them in the absence of a bylaw or special rule of order that specifically grants another body that authority."

## Domain 6: Being and Serving as a Professional Parliamentarian and Teaching Parliamentary Procedure

**1.** _Stated in section (MCQ)_ — Which of the following statements appears in RONR (12th ed.) 63:38?

   A. Exceptions to the rule that minutes are approved at the next regular meeting (or at the next meeting within the session) arise when the next meeting will not be held within a quarterly time interval, when the term of a specified portion of the membership will expire before the start of the next meeting, or when, as at…
   B. At a mass meeting, the “membership” consists of all persons in the invited category who attend.
   C. An example of a simple resolution expressing an opinion or position of an organized society is given in 10:3.
   D. In some professional societies and other organizations where particular aspects of discipline are of special importance, the handling of such matters is simplified by providing in the bylaws for a standing Committee on Discipline (see 50, 56).

   C. **12.** _Stated in section (MCQ)_ — Which of the following statements appears in RONR (12th ed.) 63:32?

   C. So, if the chair ignores a member seeking the floor while entitled to it, ignores a properly made nondilatory motion, “gavels through” a motion in an improper attempt to cut off debate, or violates any other rule, any member may immediately raise a Point of Order.
   D. A small local organization should rarely require the services of a parliamentarian, unless it undertakes a general revision of its bylaws; but for large assemblies and conventions or organizations where the transaction of business is apt to be complex, it is advisable to engage one.

## Domain 7: Boards and Committees, and Writing and Interpreting Bylaws

**1.** _Stated in section (MCQ)_ — Which of the following statements appears in RONR (12th ed.) 50:23?

   A. Less frequently, it may become desirable to apply a similar process to something already adopted—as bylaws, a program, or a resolution.
   B. All of the meetings of a special committee constitute one session (8).
   C. After the call to order and before the reading of the minutes, the next two headings may be included:
   D. In a committee of the whole or its variations (52), the quorum is the same as in the assembly unless the rules of the assembly or the organization (that is, either its bylaws or its rules of order) specify otherwise.

**2.** _Quote → section (MCQ)_ — From which section of RONR (12th ed.) is the following?

   "In stating the question, the chair should make sure that those present understand the means by which the assembly can modify the proposals contained in the resolutions (see 10:29–30), and should provide such explanations as he believes necessary."

   A. 21:2
   B. 50:14
   C. 53:17
   D. 21:9

**3.** _Stated in section (MCQ)_ — Which of the following statements appears in RONR (12th ed.) 50:21?

   A. When a committee has been appointed, its chairman (or first-named member temporarily acting—see 13:18) should call it together.
   B. Although the chair has no authority to impose a penalty or to order the offending member removed from the hall, the assembly has that power.
   C. Each of these three devices is best suited to assemblies of a particular range in size and provides a different degree of protection against disorderliness and its possible consequences—which are risked when each member is allowed to speak an unlimited number of times in debate, such risk increasing in proportion to…
   D. Aside from these principles, there is no single, all-inclusive test for determining when a proposed amendment is germane and when it is not.

**4.** _Cloze recall_ — Fill in the blank: Although it is possible for a report, in the circumstances just described, to present recommendations which are not in the form of resolutions or motions, the “adoption” of such recommendations by the parent assembly may, depending on their wording or that of the motion to adopt, lead to confusion as to whether their adoption authorizes _____ or only has the force of a declaration of intent (requiring the adoption of subsequent resolutions for implementation).

**5.** _Stated in section (MCQ)_ — Which of the following statements appears in RONR (12th ed.) 59:64?

   A. As an example of a motion to strike out and insert, assume that the following resolution is pending:
   B. The object of a nominating ballot is to provide the members with an indication of the sentiments of the voting body, which they may take into account in voting in the election.
   C. In the foregoing connection it should be noted that the consideration of a matter that was referred to a board or committee cannot be objected to (26) when it is reported on— regardless of whether the matter was referred as a pending question (13) or as a subject on which no question was pending.
   D. Printed or reproduced material assembled in cooperation with the Program Committee for distribution to the delegates in advance of the convention should include directions for getting to the convention by the various means of transportation available, and information about the locality, points of interest,…

**6.** _Stated in section (MCQ)_ — Which of the following statements appears in RONR (12th ed.) 51:35?

   A. Introduction of Subsidiary or Incidental Motions as a Part of—or Privileged Motions as an Interruption of—the Consideration of a Main Motion.
   B. It is the right of every member who notices a breach of the rules to insist on their enforcement.
   C. A society has no executive board, nor can its officers act as a board, except as the bylaws may provide; and when so established, the board has only such power as is delegated to it by the bylaws or by vote of the society’s assembly referring individual matters to it.
   D. The resolution is treated as any other main question, just as in the preceding case dealing with the recommendation of a standing committee.

**7.** _Quote → section (MCQ)_ — From which section of RONR (12th ed.) is the following?

   "The complete rules governing committees of the whole, proceedings in quasi committee of the whole, and informal consideration are given below."

   A. 52:3
   B. 23:6
   C. 10:24
   D. 27:8

**8.** _Stated in section (MCQ)_ — Which of the following statements appears in RONR (12th ed.) 51:43?

   A. Committees of organized societies operate under the bylaws, the parliamentary authority, and any special rules of order or standing rules of the society which may be applicable to them.
   B. Prior to or during a convention, members of a delegation may need or wish to meet as a group to decide how they will act with reference to certain matters to come before the convention; a meeting of this kind is usually called a caucus.
   C. When a point of order is submitted to a vote of the assembly and the point relates to stopping something from being done, it is usually best to put the question so that an affirmative vote will be in favor of allowing the proceedings to continue as if the point had not been raised.
   D. As in the preceding case, no motions are necessary, and the chair states the question first on the amendment, and after it is voted on, then on the resolution.

   C. In reference to an order of business specially adopted for a given session, the term program is often used instead of agenda; but while the latter technically includes only items of business, the former may include also the times for speakers, meals, and other nonbusiness matters.
   D. In rare instances after an assembly has received a report, it may have occasion to adopt the (entire) report; an affirmative vote on such a motion has the effect of the assembly’s endorsing every word of the report —including the indicated facts and the reasoning—as its own statement (see also 10:52–53).

   D. After the presentation of the report of an officer, a board, or a committee, one or more motions to carry out recommendations contained in the report may be introduced.

**219.** _Stated in section (MCQ)_ — Which of the following statements appears in RONR (12th ed.) 51:3?

   D. During a meeting the work of the parliamentarian should be limited to giving advice to the chair and, when requested, to any other member.

**Answer Key**

1. Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [50:23](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-50-23) — "All of the meetings of a special committee constitute one session (8)."
2. Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [53:17](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-53-17) — "In stating the question, the chair should make sure that those present understand the means by which the assembly can modify the proposals contained in the resolutions (see 10:29–30), and should provide such explanations as he believes necessary."
